Features: Rasa NLU (natural language understanding) for intent classification & entity extraction, Rasa Core for dialogue management, and lots of customization – you can inject custom Python code at any step. 
Rasa（開放原始碼）– 一個用來建立自訂對話式 AI 聊天機器人的開放原始碼框架。Rasa 是一個以開發者為導向的工具組：你可以定義意圖、實體與對話規則（或使用機器學習政策來學習對話）。它提供完整的控制權，且可以自架設，因此資料會留在本地端。功能包括：Rasa NLU（自然語言理解）用於意圖分類與實體抽取、Rasa Core 用於對話管理，以及許多自訂選項 – 你可以在任何階段插入自訂的 Python 程式碼。
    

    

      Pricing: 
      Rasa Open Source is free to use (Apache 2.0 license). They offer Rasa Pro/Enterprise, which includes a managed platform, enterprise-grade analytics, and support. Rasa Enterprise is a paid subscription typically negotiated per production instance or chatbot. (They introduced a “free Rasa Pro” license for one bot with up to 1k monthly conversations to entice companies; beyond that, it’s paid)​
      . 
價格：Rasa Open Source 可免費使用（Apache 2.0 授權條款）。他們提供 Rasa Pro/Enterprise，包含管理平台、企業等級的分析功能與支援。Rasa Enterprise 是一種付費訂閱方案，通常依生產實例或聊天機器人的數量進行協議。他們曾推出「免費 Rasa Pro」授權，適用於最多一個機器人且每月最多 1,000 次對話的情況，以吸引企業使用；超過此範圍則需付費。
    

    

      Large enterprises can expect to pay for support and scaling – but Rasa doesn’t disclose rates publicly. The key point is that if you have in-house developers, Rasa lets you build without licensing costs, and then you only pay if you need official support or their enterprise dashboard. Many academic projects use Rasa for free, and some companies run Rasa OS on their infrastructure to avoid SaaS fees.
大型企業預期會為支援與擴展功能付費，但 Rasa 並未公開收費標準。重點在於，如果你有內部開發人員，Rasa 讓你以無授權費用的方式進行開發，僅在需要官方支援或企業版看板時才需付費。許多學術專案都免費使用 Rasa，一些公司則在其基礎設施上運行 Rasa OS 以避免 SaaS 費用。
    

    

      11. Education and Research AI Tools
11. 教育與研究 AI 工具 
    

    

      Elicit (by Ought) –
Elicit（由 Ought 開發）–
    

    

       
      An AI research assistant tool that helps scholars and learners find relevant papers and answer research questions. Elicit allows a user to input a natural language question (especially ones that would be answered by academic literature, e.g., “What are the effects of X on Y according to recent studies?”). It then uses language models and a paper corpus (papers from Semantic Scholar) to find relevant publications and summarize the findings​. It also can brainstorm research ideas or summarize a given paper. 
一個協助學者與學習者尋找相關論文並回答研究問題的 AI 研究助理工具。Elicit 讓使用者輸入自然語言問題（尤其是那些會由學術文獻回答的問題，例如：「根據最近的研究，X 對 Y 有什麼影響？」）。它隨後會使用語言模型與論文資料庫（來自 Semantic Scholar 的論文）來尋找相關出版品並總結研究結果。它也能協助產生研究點子或總結指定的論文。
    

    

      Features: 
      literature review assistance – it surfaces not just keyword matches. Still, it looks at the context (thanks to the LLM), semantic paper search, and a tool to compare snippets from multiple papers answering the question. Pricing: Elicit is free to use. It’s a nonprofit research lab (Ought) project, and they’ve kept it open for the community. (No login required; heavy users can create a free account to save searches.) Since grants fund it, academics benefit from full access at no cost. This makes it a popular experimental tool for quick paper discovery in graduate student circles.
功能：文獻回顧協助 – 它不僅僅顯示關鍵字匹配，同時也會考量上下文（感謝 LLM 的協助），語義化的論文搜尋，以及一個比較多篇論文片段回答同一問題的工具。價格：Elicit 可以免費使用。它是非營利研究實驗室（Ought）的專案，他們將其對社群開放。 （無需登入；重度使用者可以建立免費帳號來儲存搜尋。）由於有研究經費支撐，學術界可以免費使用完整功能。這使得它成為研究生圈中快速發現論文的熱門實驗工具。
    

    

      Semantic Scholar & AI-powered features – 
      Semantic Scholar is an academic search engine (by Allen Institute for AI) indexes over 200 million papers. 
語義學者與 AI 功能 – Semantic Scholar 是一個學術搜尋引擎（由 Allen Institute for AI 開發），索引超過 2 億篇論文。
    

    

      It has incorporated AI in features like TL;DR summaries (automatically generated one-sentence summaries of papers) and a semantic recommendation system (“similar papers”). It also recently introduced Semantic Reader with Co-Pilot, an experimental PDF reader that shows an AI sidebar answering questions about the paper, explaining acronyms, and summarizing sections – effectively using an LLM fine-tuned scientific text. 
它已整合 AI 功能，例如 TL;DR 摘要（自動生成的論文單句摘要）和語義推薦系統（「相似論文」）。它最近也推出了 Semantic Reader 搭配 Co-Pilot，這是一個實驗性的 PDF 閱讀器，會顯示一個 AI 側邊欄來回答與論文相關的問題、解釋縮寫以及摘要各個段落 – 有效地使用了一個針對科學文獻微調的 LLM。
    

    

      Pricing: Semantic Scholar is free for researchers. The AI features (summaries, etc.) are provided openly. The Semantic Reader AI Co-Pilot is in beta (available for select papers via a waitlist or partnership, e.g., with arXiv papers). Academic institutions might collaborate with AI2 for broader access, but currently, it’s all free as it’s a research initiative.
價格：Semantic Scholar 對研究者是免費的。AI 功能（如摘要等）皆公開提供。Semantic Reader 的 AI Co-Pilot 目前處於測試階段（僅部分論文透過等候名單或合作夥伴提供，例如與 arXiv 合作的論文）。學術機構可能與 AI2 合作以獲得更廣泛的使用權，但目前所有功能皆為免費，因為這是一個研究計畫。
    

    

      Scite – 
      An AI tool for analyzing scientific citation statements. Scite lets you see how a paper is cited by later papers – specifically; it uses NLP to classify whether citations are supporting, contrasting, or just mentioning the referenced work. This helps researchers quickly gauge the 
      reputation or impact
       of a paper’s findings (e.g. if multiple later studies 
      contradict
       the original claim). 
Scite – 一個用來分析科學文獻引用語句的 AI 工具。Scite 讓你看到一篇論文是如何被後續文獻引用的，特別是它使用自然語言處理技術來分類引用是支持、反駁，或是僅提及被引用的文獻。這有助於研究者快速評估一篇論文的聲譽或影響力（例如，若有多篇後續研究反駁原始論點）。
    

    

      Scite also has an AI assistant feature. You can ask a question, and it will try to answer with evidence from papers (providing cited sources). Pricing: Scite has a free tier (limited number of citation look-ups per month). 
Scite 還有 AI 助理的功能。你可以提出問題，它會嘗試以文獻中的證據來回答（並提供被引用的來源）。價格：Scite 提供免費層（每月有限制的引用查詢次數）。
    

    

      Premium personal plans are about $10/month for academics (for unlimited site reports and AI assistant queries). Institutional licenses are available for libraries (so students and faculty can all use them under the university IP range). The value for paying is in terms of extensive usage and API access. 
高階個人方案約為每月 10 美元，適用於學術研究者（提供無限制的網站報告與 AI 助理查詢）。機構授權則可供圖書館使用（讓學生與教職員工都能在大學 IP 範圍內使用）。付費的價值在於廣泛使用與 API 存取。
    

    

      For casual use, the free account (up to ~5 AI answers and 100 citation searches per month) might suffice, but active researchers may subscribe to get unlimited access.
對於輕度使用，免費帳號（每月最多約 5 次 AI 回答與 100 次引用查詢）可能已經足夠，但積極從事研究的學者可能選擇訂閱以獲得無限制的使用權。
    

    

      ChatGPT (for educational use) – 
      Many students and researchers use general LLMs like ChatGPT or Claude to assist with studying or research in various ways: explaining complex concepts, generating quiz questions, translating passages, proofreading, brainstorming thesis ideas, summarizing articles, etc. 
ChatGPT（用於教育用途）– 很多學生與研究者會使用像 ChatGPT 或 Claude 這類一般的 LLMs 來協助學習或研究，方式包括解釋複雜概念、產生測驗題目、翻譯段落、校對、腦力激盪論文點子、總結文章等。
    

    

      While we discussed ChatGPT in general earlier, it’s worth noting that in the academic context, it’s free for essential use, which has led to broad adoption among students. The ChatGPT Plus ($20/mo) is often used by researchers who need the more advanced GPT-4 model for better accuracy in technical topics or need access even during peak times. 
雖然我們之前已經討論過 ChatGPT 的一般用途，但值得一提的是，在學術環境中，它對基本用途是免費的，這使得學生廣泛採用。ChatGPT Plus（$20/月）則常被研究者使用，他們需要更先進的 GPT-4 模型以提高技術主題的準確性，或是在高峰時間仍能使用。
    

    

      OpenAI also offers GPT-4 API (at ~$ $0.03/1K tokens for input and $0.06/1K output), which some academic developers use to build custom research assistant tools. OpenAI has even announced a ChatGPT Education Pilot (ChatGPT Edu) for campuses with discounted rates​. So, while not an academic-specific tool, ChatGPT is de facto an important AI tool in education.
OpenAI 也提供 GPT-4 API（輸入約$0.03/1K tokens，輸出約$0.06/1K tokens），有些學術開發者會用來建立自訂的研究助理工具。OpenAI 甚至宣布了一個 ChatGPT 教育試點計畫（ChatGPT Edu），為校園提供折扣價格。因此，雖然 ChatGPT 不是專為學術設計的工具，但它已成為教育領域事實上的重要 AI 工具。
    

    

      Khanmigo (Khan Academy) –
       An AI tutor integrated into Khan Academy’s platform, powered by GPT-4. Khanmigo can be a student tutor (answering questions step-by-step without giving away the answer, guiding learning) or an educator teaching assistant (helping draft lesson plans or create quizzes). 
Khanmigo（Khan Academy）– 一個整合於 Khan Academy 平台的 AI 導師，由 GPT-4 驅動。Khanmigo 可以作為學生導師（逐步回答問題而不直接透露答案，引導學習）或教育者教學助理（協助擬定課程計畫或建立測驗）。 
    

    

      Use cases: Students stuck on a math problem can ask Khanmigo for help, and Khanmigo will try to coach them to the solution with hints. It can also role-play as characters for learning (e.g., a historical figure for a student to interview in history class). Pricing/
使用情境：學生卡在數學問題上時，可以向 Khanmigo 求助，Khanmigo 會嘗試透過提示引導學生找到解答。它也可以扮演角色來促進學習（例如，在歷史課上扮演歷史人物，讓學生進行訪問）。 
    

    

      Availability: Currently, Khanmigo is in a pilot phase—available to a limited number of users. Initially, access was given to donors who contribute $20/month to Khan Academy, but Khan Academy recently announced that Khanmigo will open up more broadly at around $4/month for individuals (and free for certain school district partnerships)​. 
可用性：目前，Khanmigo 處於試點階段，僅對有限的用戶開放。最初，只有每月捐贈 20 美元支持 Khan Academy 的捐助者才能使用，但 Khan Academy 最近宣布，Khanmigo 將在約每月 4 美元的費用下對個人用戶更廣泛開放（並對某些學區合作關係提供免費）。 
    

    

      It’s not yet freely available because they monitor and improve it. The low price indicates Khan Academy’s nonprofit approach to making AI tutoring affordable at scale once it is fully launched.
它尚未完全免費，因為他們持續監測並改進這項服務。低廉的價格顯示 Khan Academy 以非營利方式推動 AI 導師，使其在全面推出後能大規模提供經濟實惠的學習輔導。
    

    

      Quizlet (Q-Chat)—
      Quizlet, a popular study flashcard app, has integrated an AI tutor called Q-Chat. Q-Chat uses ChatGPT’s API to create an interactive tutor who quizzes the student based on Quizlet co
      ntent. 
Quizlet (Q-Chat)— Quizlet 是一款廣受歡迎的學習閃卡應用程式，已整合了一個名為 Q-Chat 的 AI 教學助手。Q-Chat 使用 ChatGPT 的 API 來建立一個互動式教學者，根據 Quizlet 的內容對學生進行測試。
    

    

      For example, suppose you have a set of flashcards on Spanish vocabulary. In that case, Q-Chat will have a back-and-forth conversation in Spanish, ask you to translate words, and give feedback – essentially turning static flashcards into a dynamic quiz game​. 
例如，假設你有一組西班牙語單字的閃卡，Q-Chat 就會以西班牙語進行來回對話，請你翻譯單字並給予反饋—基本上將靜態的閃卡轉化為動態的測驗遊戲。
    

    

      It follows a Socratic method by asking questions rather than just letting you flip flashcards​. Pricing: Quizlet is free with ads and flashcards for essential use. Q-Chat, however, is a premium feature requiring Quizlet Plus (approximately $35 per year for students). 
它採用蘇格拉底方法，透過提問來引導學習，而非只是讓你翻轉閃卡。
    

    

      Quizlet Plus removes ads and adds features like advanced learning modes – Q-Chat is included for subscribers. 
價格：Quizlet 提供免費版本，含廣告和基本的閃卡功能。然而 Q-Chat 是高階功能，需要訂閱 Quizlet Plus（學生大約每年 35 美元）。
    

    

      Since Q-Chat launched in beta in 2023, Quizlet Plus subscribers have had access to iOS (with expansion to all platforms). There’s no separate charge for Q-Chat beyond the Plus subscription.
自 2023 年 Q-Chat 進入測試版以來，Quizlet Plus 訂閱者已可使用 iOS（後擴展至所有平台）。除了 Plus 訂閱費外，Q-Chat 不另外收取費用。
    

    

      Turnitin Originality (AI writing detection) – 
      For academic integrity, it’s worth mentioning Turnitin’s AI writing detection, which many universities are using to check if student essays are AI-generated. This isn’t a tool that helps you create or study; instead, it’s an AI tool that instructors use. 
Turnitin Originality（AI 寫作檢測）－為維護學術誠信，值得一提的是 Turnitin 的 AI 寫作檢測功能，許多大學正用來檢查學生論文是否為 AI 生成。這不是幫助你學習或創作的工具，而是教師用來檢測的 AI 工具。
    

    

      Turnitin claims it can detect GPT-generated text with a certain confidence. It’s bundled in Turnitin’s plagiarism suite for institutions (pricing part of Turnitin license, not sold to individuals).
Turnitin 聲稱可以以一定程度的確定性檢測 GPT 生成的文本。此功能包含在 Turnitin 的抄襲檢測套件中，用於機構（價格為 Turnitin 授權的一部分，不對個人銷售）。
    

    

      It illustrates the ecosystem: as students use AI like ChatGPT, educators use AI to detect potential misuse.
這說明了生態系統：當學生使用 AI 如 ChatGPT 時，教育者則使用 AI 來檢測潛在的濫用情況。
    

    

      Jupyter Notebooks + AI—Jupyter is the classic tool
       for coding and analysis in research. Now, tools like Jupyter AI (an extension) allow using LLMs within notebooks, e.g., a magic command to explain code or generate code cells from instructions. 
Jupyter Notebooks + AI—Jupyter 是研究中編碼與分析的經典工具。現在，像 Jupyter AI（一個擴充套件）這樣的工具允許在筆記本中使用 LLMs，例如，透過魔術指令來解釋程式碼或根據指示產生程式碼區塊。
    

    

      This is experimental but shows up in academia, where data science students can get AI help directly in the environment they code. It’s open source and free (requires hooking to an API like OpenAI or local model).
這屬於實驗性質，但在學術界已出現，數據科學學生可以在他們編碼的環境中直接獲得 AI 的協助。它是開源且免費的（需要連結到像 OpenAI 或本地模型這樣的 API）。
    

    

      (Academic researchers also heavily use open-source AI frameworks (next section) to develop new AI models, but those are more about creating AI than using AI to assist in general tasks. Regarding widely available tools for academic assignments, the above covers literature review, studying, and tutoring.)
（學術研究者也大量使用開源 AI 框架（下一節）來開發新的 AI 模型，但這些更多是關於建立 AI 而非用 AI 來協助一般任務。關於廣泛可用的學術作業工具，上述內容涵蓋了文獻回顧、學習與輔導。）
    

    

      AI Development Frameworks and Open-Source Libraries
AI 開發框架與開源函式庫
    

    

      For those building AI models (in business R&D or academic research), some key frameworks and tools are widely used and freely available:  
    

    

      TensorFlow – 
      An open-source deep learning framework initially developed by Google. TensorFlow allows constructing neural networks (from simple to very large) and computation on GPUs/TPUs for acceleration. It’s used in research and production (vision, NLP, etc.).   
    

    

      Features: 
      It supports high-level APIs like Keras for ease of use and lower-level ops for custom model building. It has a rich ecosystem (TensorBoard for visualization, TensorFlow Lite for mobile, etc.).   
    

    

      Pricing:
       TensorFlow is entirely free and open-source (Apache 2.0 license). It requires computing resources—which one might pay for in the cloud or invest in GPUs—but the software is inexpensive. It’s heavily used in academia (many ML courses use TensorFlow/Keras) and industry (Google uses it internally, and others use it in products).  
    

    

      PyTorch – 
      Another open-source deep learning library, initially by Facebook (Meta). PyTorch has become very popular in research due to its dynamic computation graph (which feels more like regular Python code) and intuitive API. It’s widely used in cutting-edge AI developments (most NLP breakthrough models, like transformers, were first implemented in PyTorch). Features: strong support for GPU acceleration, a large set of built-in neural network layers and loss functions, and a growing ecosystem (e.g., PyTorch Lightning for easier training loops).   
    

    

      Pricing: 
      PyTorch is free and open-source (BSD-style license). There are no fees. Many companies (NVIDIA, Microsoft, etc.) contribute to it. Like TensorFlow, the cost only comes from hardware. As an example of impact, almost all computer vision and NLP researchers will know and possibly use PyTorch—it’s that prevalent.  
    

    

      scikit-learn – 
      A classic machine learning library in Python for traditional ML (not neural networks). Scikit-learn implements algorithms like logistic regression, random forests, SVM, clustering, etc., plus tools for model evaluation and data preprocessing.   
    

    

      It’s a staple for any data scientist’s toolkit and is excellent for smaller datasets and straightforward ML tasks. Pricing: sci-kit-learn is free (BSD license). It’s often taught in data science classes and used in production for interpretable models or as a baseline.  
    

    

      Hugging Face Hub & Transformers—Hugging Face is an open platform and library that has revolutionized NLP and beyond by sharing pre-trained AI models. The Transformers library by Hugging Face provides easy interfaces for using
       state-of-the-art models (like BERT, GPT-2/3, T5, Stable Diffusion, etc.) for tasks such as text classification, Q&A, translation, and text generation​.   
    

    

      Meanwhile, the Hugging Face Hub is an online repository with over 1 million models hosted by the community (and datasets and demos)​. Features: With a few lines of code, one can download and fine-tune a pre-trained model to their data.   
    

    

      The hub also hosts spaces (live demo apps) so researchers can show off models. Pricing: The libraries (Transformers, Diffusers, etc.) are free and open-source.   
    

    

      The Hub is free for open models/datasets. Hugging Face’s business model involves offering paid enterprise features, like private model hosting, increased API rate limits, and team collaboration accounts. They offer a hosted inference API where you pay per call for a fully managed model-as-a-service (pricing varies by model size). 
The Hub 對於開放模型/資料集是免費的。Hugging Face 的商業模式涉及提供付費企業功能，例如私人模型主機、提高 API 請求上限，以及團隊協作帳號。他們提供一個托管推論 API，您可按每次呼叫付費使用完整的模型即服務 (價格因模型大小而異)。
    

    

      However, the HF ecosystem is free for most academics and developers unless they opt into their paid services. This has dramatically lowered the barrier to entry for using advanced AI models.
然而，HF 生態系統對於大多數學者和開發者來說是免費的，除非他們選擇使用其付費服務。這大幅降低了使用先進 AI 模型的門檻。
    

    

      Jupyter Notebooks – 
      While not an AI algorithm, Jupyter is the de facto environment for many data scientists and researchers to experiment with AI. It’s an interactive notebook that can contain code, text, and results – great for exploration and teaching. 
Jupyter Notebooks – 雖然 Jupyter 不是 AI 算法，但它是許多資料科學家和研究者實驗 AI 的事實上標準環境。它是一個互動式筆記本，可以包含程式碼、文字和結果 – 非常適合探索與教學。
    

    

      Pricing
      : Jupyter is open-source and free (many use it locally or via free cloud like Google Colab). Google Colab, specifically, gives a free cloud GPU environment for running small AI experiments, which has been very important for students worldwide who don’t have local GPUs. (Colab Pro exists at ~$10/month for better resources, but the free tier suffices for many coursework.)
價格 : Jupyter 是開源且免費的 (許多使用者會在本地或透過免費雲端如 Google Colab 使用)。Google Colab 特別提供免費的雲端 GPU 環境，用於執行小型 AI 實驗，這對全球缺乏本地 GPU 的學生來說非常重要。(Colab Pro 約為每月 $10，提供更好的資源，但免費版已足夠許多課程使用。)
    

    

      LangChain – 
      An open-source framework for building applications around language models (LLMs). It provides utilities to chain prompts together, manage conversation memory, and connect LLMs with other tools (APIs, databases). It’s become popular for those developing custom chatbots or “GPT agents.” Pricing: LangChain is free to use (Python/JS library). It requires access to an LLM (which might be via an API that costs money or an open model). Some LangChain-supporting platforms (like LlamaIndex) have free/community versions too.
LangChain – 一個開放原始碼的框架，用於在語言模型（LLMs）周圍建立應用程式。它提供工具，用於串接提示、管理對話記憶，並連接 LLMs 與其他工具（APIs、資料庫）。它已成為開發自訂聊天機器人或「GPT 代理人」的熱門選擇。價格：LangChain 可免費使用（Python/JS 套件）。它需要存取 LLM（這可能是透過收費的 API 或開放模型）。一些支援 LangChain 的平台（如 LlamaIndex）也有免費/社群版。
    

    

      (These frameworks highlight that the development tools for AI are largely open-source – a researcher or startup doesn’t pay for TensorFlow or PyTorch themselves. Instead, cost arises from hardware.
（這些框架顯示出 AI 的開發工具大多是開放原始碼的 – 研究人員或新創公司不需要自行付費取得 TensorFlow 或 PyTorch。相反地，成本來自於硬體。
    

    

      (GPUs from NVIDIA, cloud TPUs, etc.) or from using proprietary models via API (like OpenAI). Cloud platforms also offer managed versions of these frameworks: e.g., Google’s Vertex AI or AWS Sagemaker can run TensorFlow/PyTorch jobs with a convenience fee on top of compute. 
（NVIDIA 的 GPU、雲端 TPUs 等）或來自於透過 API 使用專有模型（如 OpenAI）。雲端平台也提供這些框架的管理版本：例如，Google 的 Vertex AI 或 AWS Sagemaker 可以運行 TensorFlow/PyTorch 作業，並在計算資源上收取便利費用。
    

    

      However, one could avoid that by managing one’s servers. Thus, from a cost perspective, The “knowledge” (code) is free, and the “execution” (compute) is what you budget for.)
然而，透過管理自己的伺服器，可以避免這些費用。因此，從成本的角度來看，「知識」（程式碼）是免費的，而「執行」（計算資源）才是需要預算的部分。）
    

    

      Enterprise AI Platforms (Cloud AI Services)
企業 AI 平台 (雲端 AI 服務)
    

    

      Major tech companies offer broad AI and machine learning services on their cloud platforms, catering to enterprise developers who want to infuse AI without building everything from scratch:
主要科技公司在其雲端平台上提供廣泛的 AI 與機器學習服務，以協助企業開發者在不從頭開始建立所有系統的情況下，融入 AI 功能：
    

    

      Microsoft Azure AI Services –
       Azure offers a range of pre-built AI APIs under Cognitive Services, e.g., Computer Vision API (for image recognition, OCR), Speech-to-text and Text-to-speech, Language Understanding (LUIS), Translator, and Anomaly Detector. These let developers call an API and get AI results without training a model. Azure also provides the Azure OpenAI Service, giving enterprise access to OpenAI’s GPT-4, GPT-3, and DALL-E models with Azure’s security and compliance (this is how many companies integrate ChatGPT-like capabilities). Azure has a Machine Learning studio for training and deploying models for custom ML and a managed environment for notebooks and AutoML. 
微軟 Azure AI 服務 – Azure 提供多種預建的 AI API，屬於 Cognitive Services，例如：影像辨識 API（用於影像辨識、OCR）、語音轉文字與文字轉語音、語言理解（LUIS）、翻譯器與異常偵測器。這些服務讓開發者只需呼叫 API，即可取得 AI 結果，而無需訓練模型。Azure 還提供 Azure OpenAI 服務，讓企業可以使用 OpenAI 的 GPT-4、GPT-3 和 DALL-E 模型，並搭配 Azure 的安全性與合規性（這也是許多公司整合類似 ChatGPT 功能的方式）。Azure 並設有機器學習工作室，用於訓練與部署自訂的機器學習模型，以及提供筆記本和 AutoML 的管理環境。
    

    

      Pricing:
       Cognitive Services are pay-per-use (e.g., ~$1 per 1,000 text analytics calls or $1.5 per 1,000 speech seconds transcribed – prices vary by region). Azure OpenAI is charged per 1K tokens (similar to OpenAI’s pricing). Azure ML training uses compute instances charged per hour (depending on VM type). There are no up-front fees; enterprises pay for what they use, often negotiating discounts. As a reference, if using GPT-4 via Azure, it’s around $0.06 per 1K tokens (output) – same as OpenAI, plus maybe a slight premium for Azure’s enterprise handling.
計費：Cognitive Services 是按使用量計費（例如，每 1,000 個文字分析呼叫約 ~$1 或每 1,000 個轉錄語音秒數 $1.5 – 價格會因地區而異）。Azure OpenAI 是按 1,000 個 token 計費（與 OpenAI 的計費方式類似）。Azure ML 訓練使用計算實例，按小時計費（視 VM 類型而定）。沒有預付費用；企業只需為實際使用的服務付款，通常會談判折扣。作為參考，若使用 Azure 的 GPT-4，每 1,000 個 token（輸出）約為 $0.06 – 與 OpenAI 相同，加上 Azure 對企業處理的輕微附加費用。
    

    

      Google Cloud Vertex AI – 
      Google’s unified AI platform Vertex AI provides pretrained API services and tools to build custom models. Pretrained APIs include Vision AI (image recognition, OCR), Speech-to-Text and Text-to-Speech, Translation, Natural Language (for entity extraction, sentiment), Cloud Vision Product Search, etc. 
Google Cloud Vertex AI – Google 的統一 AI 平台 Vertex AI 提供預訓練的 API 服務和工具，用於建立自訂模型。預訓練的 API 包括 Vision AI（影像辨識、OCR）、語音轉文字與文字轉語音、翻譯、自然語言（用於實體抽取、情感分析）、Cloud Vision Product Search 等。
    

    

      They have Dialogflow CX for chatbots (as covered). For custom development, Vertex AI has AutoML (where Google will train a model on your data for vision, text, or tabular prediction tasks) – this was earlier branded AutoML Vision, AutoML Tables, etc. – and also offers Notebooks, training pipelines, feature store, and model deployment in one place. 
他們有 Dialogflow CX 用於聊天機器人（如前所述）。針對自訂開發，Vertex AI 提供 AutoML（Google 會根據您的資料訓練模型，用於影像、文字或表格預測任務）——這項服務先前分別以 AutoML Vision、AutoML Tables 等品牌推出——並在同一平台提供筆記本、訓練流程、特徵倉庫與模型部署。
    

    

      Pricing: Similar to Azure, Google’s AI APIs are pay-as-you-go. For example, Vision OCR might be ~$1.50 per 1,000 pages; Natural Language analyzes text ~$1 per 1,000 text records, and Translation $20 per million characters. 
價格：與 Azure 類似，Google 的 AI API 是按使用量計費。例如，Vision OCR 約為每 1,000 頁 $1.50；自然語言分析文字約為每 1,000 個文字記錄 $1，翻譯則為每一百萬個字元 $20。
    

    

      Vertex AutoML training costs depend on computing hours used (and model type). Google often provides $300 free credit for new cloud users, which can be used for these services. For large enterprise deals, Google Cloud will work out committed spend discounts. Google also now offers Model Garden (to access Google’s models like PaLM 2 via Vertex AI) – e.g., PaLM 2 text-bison model priced at ~$3 per 1K input tokens and $8 per 1K output tokens (that’s their GPT-4 competitor model cost). 
Vertex AutoML 訓練費用取決於使用的計算小時數（以及模型類型）。Google 通常會為新雲端用戶提供 $300 的免費信用額，可用於這些服務。對於大型企業合作案，Google Cloud 會計算承諾支出的折扣。Google 現在也提供 Model Garden（透過 Vertex AI 使用 Google 的模型，例如 PaLM 2）——例如，PaLM 2 的 text-bison 模型價格為每 1,000 個輸入 token 約 $3，每 1,000 個輸出 token 約 $8（這是他們 GPT-4 的競爭模型的費用）。
    

    

      All said enterprises can pick and choose – e.g., just using Cloud Vision API lightly might cost tens of dollars a month, whereas an entire Vertex AI pipeline training big models could run into thousands.
企業皆可自由選擇 – 例如，僅輕度使用 Cloud Vision API 月費可能就達數十美元，而完整的 Vertex AI 管線用來訓練大型模型，費用可能高達數千美元。
    

    

      AWS AI/ML Services – 
      Amazon’s cloud has a broad set: at the API level, Amazon Rekognition for image and video analysis (face recognition, moderation, text in images), Amazon Comprehend for NLP (entity, sentiment, medical text analysis), Amazon Polly for text-to-speech (with many voices), Transcribe for speech-to-text, Translate, Lex for chatbots (as covered), and Amazon Forecast for time-series predictions, etc. They also offer AWS SageMaker, a comprehensive service to build, train, and deploy custom ML models. 
AWS AI/ML 服務 – Amazon 的雲端服務包含廣泛的選項：在 API 層面，有 Amazon Rekognition 用於影像與影片分析（臉部辨識、內容審核、影像中的文字），Amazon Comprehend 用於自然語言處理（實體辨識、情感分析、醫療文書分析），Amazon Polly 用於文字轉語音（支援多種語音），Transcribe 用於語音轉文字，Translate，Lex 用於聊天機器人（如前所述），以及 Amazon Forecast 用於時間序列預測等。他們也提供 AWS SageMaker，這是一個完整的服務，用於建立、訓練與部署自訂的機器學習模型。
    

    

      SageMaker includes Studio IDE, AutoPilot (AutoML), and many built-in algorithms – plus managed Spot instances to reduce cost. Pricing: Again, per-request for the APIs (e.g., Rekognition ~$1 per 1,000 image labels, Comprehend ~$0.0001 per 100 chars processed, etc.), and hourly for SageMaker instances. SageMaker has many components: training jobs priced per instance-hours (with different rates for CPU and GPU types), model deployment priced per instance-hour of the endpoint, plus some storage. 
SageMaker 包含 Studio IDE、AutoPilot（AutoML）以及許多內建的演算法，再加上管理的 Spot 實例以降低成本。價格：同樣是按請求計費的 API（例如 Rekognition 約每 1,000 張圖片標籤 $1，Comprehend 約每處理 100 個字元 $0.0001，等等），以及按小時計費的 SageMaker 實例。SageMaker 有許多組成部分：訓練作業按實例小時計費（CPU 和 GPU 類型有不同的費用率），模型部署按端點的實例小時計費，再加上一些儲存空間。
    

    

      For example, training a medium vision model on a 
      ml.p3.2xlarge
       (with one Tesla V100 GPU) might cost ~$3.9/hour, so a 10-hour job is $39. Deploying a model on a 
      ml.m5.xlarge
       might be $0.20/hour ($144/month if 24/7). AWS has Free tier limits (like the first million characters for Comprehend free, 60 minutes per month free transcribing, etc., for 12 months). They also offer savings plans for sustained SageMaker use.
例如，使用 ml.p3.2xlarge（含一塊 Tesla V100 GPU）來訓練一個中等視覺模型，每小時約 $3.9，因此 10 小時的作業費用為 $39。將模型部署在 ml.m5.xlarge 上，每小時 $0.20（若 24 小時運行，每月約 $144）。AWS 提供免費層限制（例如 Comprehend 的前一百萬字元免費，每月免費轉譯六十分鐘，等等，持續十二個月）。他們也提供節省計劃，用於持續使用 SageMaker。
    

    

      IBM Watson X – 
      IBM’s modern AI and data platform (Watson reimagined). It includes Watsonx.ai (a studio for foundation models and ML, including access to some of IBM’s large language models and open models like LLaMA2), Watsonx. Data (data store for AI workloads), and Watson. Governance (toolkit for AI model governance and transparency). 
IBM Watson X – IBM 的現代 AI 與資料平台（Watson 重新設計的版本）。它包含 Watsonx.ai（一個用於基礎模型和機器學習的開發工作室，包括對 IBM 部分大型語言模型和開放模型（如 LLaMA2）的存取權），Watsonx. Data（用於 AI 工作負載的資料儲存），以及 Watson. Governance（用於 AI 模型治理與透明度的工具組）。
    

    

      IBM still offers Watson APIs for language, vision, etc. For instance, Watson Natural Language Understanding and Watson Discovery (which does smart document search) are available. Pricing: IBM’s cloud services are typically subscription or usage-based, similar to others. 
IBM 仍然提供 Watson APIs 用於語言、視覺等領域。例如，Watson 自然語言理解與 Watson 發現（用於智慧文件搜尋）仍然可用。價格：IBM 的雲端服務通常採用訂閱或使用量計費，與其他服務商類似。
    

    

      For example, Watson Discovery might be priced by the number of documents indexed and query volume (e.g., it starts at a few hundred $/month). IBM targets enterprise deals, often bundling Watson’s capabilities in larger digital transformation contracts. 
例如，Watson 發現的價格可能根據索引文件數量和查詢量來計算（例如，起價為數百美元/月）。IBM 的目標是企業合作案，經常將 Watson 的功能整合至較大的數位轉型合約中。
    

    

      Watsonx.ai is new so that IBM might work closely with clients on custom pricing (like a fixed price for a certain number of model training hours and deployments). As IBM’s offerings are less transparent than Azure/GCP/AWS, customers usually engage IBM or an IBM partner for quotes.
Watsonx.ai 是新推出的，因此 IBM 可能會與客戶密切合作，針對特定需求提供客製化價格（例如，固定價格包含一定數量的模型訓練小時與部署）。由於 IBM 的服務透明度較 Azure/GCP/AWS 低，客戶通常會與 IBM 或其合作夥伴洽談報價。
    

    

      Oracle AI—Oracle’s cloud also provides AI services (Vision, Speech, NLP) and an AutoML service. Oracle often includes some AI features in its
       Fusion apps as well. 
Oracle AI—Oracle 的雲端也提供 AI 服務（Vision、Speech、NLP）以及 AutoML 服務。Oracle 有時也會在其 Fusion 應用中包含一些 AI 功能。
    

    

      They are priced similarly to others (per use or per instance hour). Oracle’s differentiator is often in specific industry-trained models (e.g., manufacturing quality inspection with their Vision service).
它們的價格與其他服務類似（按使用次數或每小時實例計算）。Oracle 的差異化在於特定產業訓練的模型（例如，透過其 Vision 服務進行製造業的品質檢測）。
    

    

      SAP AI – 
      SAP integrates AI into its business software (e.g., SAP AI Business Services like Document Information Extraction for invoices or Cash Application matching). 
SAP AI – SAP 將 AI 整合至其業務軟體中（例如，SAP AI Business Services，如發票的文件資訊抽取或現金申請匹配）。
    

    

      These are often part of the SAP application license rather than standalone, though SAP does offer some AI APIs on SAP BTP (Business Technology Platform). Pricing would align with SAP’s enterprise software model (usually user-based or document-count-based add-ons).
這些功能通常包含在 SAP 應用軟體授權中，而非獨立銷售，不過 SAP 也提供一些 AI API 在 SAP BTP（Business Technology Platform）上。價格模式則與 SAP 的企業軟體模式一致（通常是基於用戶數或文件數的附加功能）。
    

    

      Open-Source & On-Prem –
       Some enterprises choose open-source stacks to avoid cloud recurring costs or for privacy. E.g., deploying OpentTS for text-to-speech internally, or LLaMA 2 model on local servers for an internal chatbot, etc. 
開源與自建 – 有些企業選擇開源架構以避免雲端的重複費用或因應隱私需求。例如，內部部署 OpentTS 進行文字轉語音，或在本地伺服器上部署 LLaMA 2 模型用於內部聊天機器人等。
    

    

      This requires more IT work but avoids per-call fees. Tools like Haystack (for building search Q&A systems with open-source models) or Jina (for neural search) are used in such scenarios. The cost is then hardware and engineering time.
這需要更多的 IT 工作，但可避免每次呼叫的費用。在這種情境下，會使用 Haystack（用於以開源模型建立搜尋問答系統）或 Jina（用於神經搜尋）等工具。成本則轉為硬體與工程時間。
    

    

      In summary, enterprise AI platforms let businesses use pre-built AI (fast to implement, pay per use) or build custom (more control, pay for compute). The pricing models are typically usage-based, which can be very cost-efficient at a small scale and grow with usage. 
總結來說，企業 AI 平台讓企業可以使用預建的 AI（快速部署，按使用計費）或自建客製化 AI（擁有更多控制權，按計算資源計費）。其計費模式通常是基於使用量，這在小規模時可以非常節省成本，並隨著使用量增加而擴展。
    

    

      Companies often evaluate ROI: e.g., does using an AI service at $0.002 per transaction save enough labor or increase revenue enough to justify that cost? If yes, adoption follows. All major cloud vendors also offer volume discounts or committed spend discounts, so big enterprises seldom pay list prices. The fierce competition among Azure, AWS, and GCP in AI benefits customers by constantly improving price performance and offering new offerings (like new model releases or special bundle deals in enterprise agreements).
企業經常評估投資回報率（ROI）：例如，使用每筆交易 $0.002 的 AI 服務，是否足以節省足夠的人力或增加足夠的營收來證明這筆成本？如果答案是肯定的，就會開始採用。所有主要的雲端服務供應商也都提供用量折扣或承諾花費折扣，因此大型企業幾乎不會支付標價。Azure、AWS 和 GCP 在 AI 方面的激烈競爭，使客戶受益，因為這促使價格表現不斷提升，並提供新的服務（例如在企業協議中推出新模型或特別組合優惠）。

      Maximizing ChatGPT: Advanced Strategies, LLM Insights, and Future Potential. Unlocking ChatGPT’s Full Potential with Prompt Engineering.
最大化 ChatGPT：進階策略、LLM 觀點與未來潛力。透過提示工程來發揮 ChatGPT 的完整潛能。
    

    

      Quality In, Quality Out:
       A key principle is that 
      ChatGPT is a mirror of your input
      . It reflects the clarity, detail, and intelligence of the prompts it’s given. As one expert puts it, “Garbage inputs? Garbage outputs. But if you feed it great inputs—elite frameworks, deep insights, and powerful prompts—it will evolve into something extraordinary”​. 
品質入，品質出：一個關鍵原則是，ChatGPT 是你輸入的鏡子。它會反映出你給予提示的清晰度、細節和智慧。正如一位專家所說：「垃圾的輸入？就會得到垃圾的輸出。但如果你給予它優質的輸入—高階框架、深入見解和強大的提示，它就會進化成非凡的東西。」​ 
    

    

      The gap between a casual query and an optimized prompt can be massive. 
隨便的查詢與優化提示之間的差距可能非常巨大。
    

    

      In fact, the only difference between an average user and a power user “isn’t the AI itself, it’s how they train it… The better your questions, the smarter your AI becomes.”​ 
事實上，普通用戶與高階用戶之間的唯一差別「不是 AI 本身，而是他們如何訓練它……你提問的品質越高，AI 就會變得越聰明。」​ 
    

    

      In practice, this means that careful prompt wording, providing context, and iterative refinement can dramatically improve ChatGPT’s performance.
實際上，這意味著仔細的提示措辭、提供情境以及反覆修訂，可以大幅提高 ChatGPT 的表現。
    

    

      Beyond “Basic” 
超越「基礎」
    

    

      Prompts:
       Using ChatGPT effectively is more than asking a question and accepting the first answer. High-level users treat it not as a magic oracle but as an interactive collaborator. Instead of a one-shot query like 
      “Explain topic X,”
       a power user might provide background, role-play a scenario, or break the task into steps. 
提示：有效使用 ChatGPT 不只是提問然後接受第一個答案。高階使用者不會把它當作一個神奇的預言者，而是視為一個互動的協作者。他們不會像「解釋主題 X」這樣一次性的提問，而是會提供背景資訊、角色扮演情境，或把任務拆解成步驟。
    

    

      For example, rather than 
      “Give me business advice,”
       one might say: 
      “Act as a veteran CEO mentor. I will describe my startup, and you will ask me probing questions to diagnose issues before giving advice.”
       This richer setup guides the AI to produce a deeper, more tailored response. 
例如，而不是直接說「給我商業建議」，可以說：「請扮演一位資深 CEO 導師。我會描述我的新創公司，而你則會問我深入的問題，診斷問題後再給建議。」這種更豐富的設定會引導 AI 產生更深入且更符合需求的回應。
    

    

      In short, stop using ChatGPT “like a toy” and start using it like an extension of your mind – the results can be transformative.
總而言之，停止將 ChatGPT 當作「玩具」使用，開始把它當作你思維的延伸 – 結果可以帶來顛覆性的改變。
    

    

      “Secret” Prompts and Techniques for Superior Results
「秘密」提示與技巧，以獲得更優秀的結果
    

    

      Advanced users have discovered certain prompt patterns (sometimes touted as “secret” prompts) that consistently yield better outputs. These aren’t magic spells, but smart strategies that any user can apply. Here are some proven techniques:
高階使用者發現某些提示模式（有時被譽為「秘密提示」）能持續產生更優質的輸出。這些並不是魔法咒語，而是任何使用者都能運用的聰明策略。以下是一些已被驗證的技巧：
    

    

      Interpretation Check:
       Before letting ChatGPT answer your request, ask it to 
      explain what you want
      . For example: 
      “Do not start writing yet. First, explain everything I asked you to do in this prompt in detail.”
       This forces the model to summarize your instructions in its own words​. 
提示檢查：在讓 ChatGPT 回答你的請求之前，請它先解釋你想要什麼。例如：「請不要開始寫作。首先，詳細說明這個提示中我要求你做的事情。」這會迫使模型用自己的話總結你的指示。
    

    

      By reviewing this, you can catch misunderstandings and correct them, aligning the AI’s interpretation with your intent (preventing those 
      “that’s not what I meant”
       moments).
透過這樣的檢查，你可以發現誤解並加以修正，使 AI 的解釋與你的意圖一致（避免那些「這不是我意思」的時刻）。
    

    

      Enforce a Human-Like Tone:
       If you need engaging, relatable writing, explicitly instruct the tone. For instance: 
      “I need this written in a human tone. Humans have fun when they write — robots don’t. Engagement is the highest priority. 
強制使用人類語氣：如果你需要生動、貼近生活的寫作，請明確指示語氣。例如：「我需要這段文字以人類的語氣來寫。人類寫東西時會很有趣，機器人則不會。互動性是最高優先順序。」
    

    

      Be conversational, empathetic, and occasionally humorous. Use idioms, metaphors, anecdotes, and natural dialogue.”
       This prompt steers ChatGPT away from sounding overly formal or “AI-like” and makes the output more lively and authentic​. 
以自然、富有同理心，偶爾帶點幽默的方式來表達。使用慣用語、比喻、小故事和自然對話。」這個提示可以讓 ChatGPT 避免過於正式或「AI 感」的語氣，使輸出內容更活潑且真實。
    

    

      It’s especially useful for creative writing, marketing copy, or any content meant for human readers.
這對創意寫作、行銷文案，或任何針對人類讀者所撰寫的內容特別有幫助。
    

    

      Prompt for Clarification Questions: 
澄清問題的提示：
    

    

      Often, we unknowingly give incomplete instructions. You can prompt ChatGPT to act like a curious collaborator by appending: 
通常我們在無意識中會給予不完整的指示。你可以透過附加以下內容，讓 ChatGPT 扮演好奇的協作者角色：
    

    

      “Before you answer, ask me any missing information you need to understand my request better.”
在回答之前，請告訴我你認為需要哪些資訊才能更好地理解我的請求。 
       
    

    

      This encourages the AI to identify gaps in your query and ask clarifying questions​. 
這會鼓勵 AI 來辨識你的問題中有哪些資訊缺口，並提出澄清問題。 
    

    

      It’s a safeguard against getting a generic or misguided answer due to missing context. By ensuring the AI has all relevant details, you’ll get a more accurate and tailored response.
這是一種防範因缺乏上下文而得到一般化或誤導性回答的機制。透過確保 AI 有所有相關資訊，你將得到更準確且符合需求的回應。 
    

    

      Self-Critique the Answer:
       
自我檢討回答：
    

    

      After ChatGPT responds, don’t move on too quickly. Ask it to critique its own answer: 
      “Criticize yourself.”
       Surprisingly, the model will often point out weaknesses or areas it could improve in its response​. 
ChatGPT 回應後，不要過快轉換話題。請它自我評估回答的內容：「自我批評。」令人驚訝的是，模型經常會在回應中指出自身的弱點或可以改進的地方。
    

    

      This self-reflection can surface new angles, correct subtle errors, or suggest refinements that you might not have considered. It’s like having the AI be its own editor – yielding a version 2.0 of the answer that is superior to the first draft.
這種自我反思能挖掘出新的觀點，糾正細微的錯誤，或提出你可能未曾考慮的改進建議。就像是讓 AI 成為自己的編輯，產生一個優於初稿的 2.0 版本回答。
    

    

      Dig Into the “Why” (Rationale Analysis):
       
深入探討「為何」（理據分析）：
    

    

      Similarly, you can ask 
      why
       ChatGPT responded as it did. 
同樣地，你也可以問為什麼 ChatGPT 會這樣回應。
    

    

      For example: 
      “Why did you write what you wrote? Provide a detailed analysis of your answer, and include suggestions for improvement based on my original prompt.”
例如：「你為何寫出這樣的回應？請詳細分析你的答案，並根據我的原始提示提供改进建議。」
       
    

    

      You can even request this in a structured form, like a table. This meta-level prompt makes the AI reveal its reasoning or assumptions and offers ways to fine-tune the result​.
你甚至可以以表格的形式要求這類結構化的回應。這種元層次提示讓 AI 揭露其思考過程或假設，並提供調整結果的方法。
    

    

      Understanding the AI’s thought process can inspire you to pose better follow-up questions or adjust your prompt for a more precise outcome.
了解 AI 的思考過程，可以啟發你提出更好的追問問題，或調整提示以獲得更精準的結果。
    

    

      Highlight Risks and Blind Spots:
       
強調風險與盲點：
    

    

      To stress-test the answer or plan you’re getting, say 
      “Before answering, list 5–10 potential risks, pitfalls, or blind spots in my request/idea.”
       This makes ChatGPT act as a devil’s advocate, identifying things you might have overlooked​.   
    

    

      It’s an experimental prompt that can uncover hidden assumptions or challenges. Once those are on the table, you can address them (either by modifying your request or asking the AI to account for those risks in its answer).  
    

    

      Ask for Examples and Analogies:
         
    

    

      If you have a draft or a piece of content from ChatGPT that feels abstract or unclear, prompt it to improve clarity.   
    

    

      For instance: 
      “Identify areas in the above text where an example, analogy, or case study would improve understanding, and suggest what to add.”  
       
    

    

      This gets the AI to review its output and pinpoint where concrete details could help​.   
    

    

      By adding illustrative examples or relatable analogies, you can significantly enhance the quality and comprehension of the final content.  
    

    

      These seven techniques are like power-tools for ChatGPT users – you can even combine them.   
    

    

      For example, you might first ask for an interpretation check (technique #1), then have the model proceed with an answer in a human tone (#2).   
    

    

      After the answer, you might invoke self-critique (#4) and then ask it to fill in examples (#7).   
    

    

      By chaining these prompts in sequence, users have reported getting outputs that are 
      “smarter, richer, and more impactful”
      ​ than what a single-pass prompt would yield.  
    

    

      Step-by-Step Reasoning (Chain-of-Thought Prompting)  
    

    

      Standard vs. chain-of-thought prompting: The model performs better on a math word problem when asked to show its reasoning (right) than when answering directly (left). In the chain-of-thought example, it breaks down the problem into steps (green text) and arrives at the correct answer​.  
    

    

      Another powerful prompting technique is to explicitly request step-by-step reasoning.   
    

    

      Complex problems (math, logic, planning tasks) often stump language models when answered in one leap. But if you say something like, 
      “Let’s think this through step by step,”
       you invoke what researchers call chain-of-thought (CoT) prompting​.   
    

    

      This tells the model to generate intermediate reasoning steps before the final answer, essentially making its hidden thought process visible. Studies have shown that inserting a simple phrase – 
      “Let’s think step by step”
       – can significantly enhance accuracy on complex reasoning tasks​.  
    

    

      Why does this help? Because large language models are trained on sequences of text, seeing a prompt that includes reasoning steps biases the model to follow that pattern. It “unlocks” reasoning abilities that might otherwise remain latent​.  
    

    

      For the user, the benefit is twofold: you get a more correct answer 
      and
       you can follow the model’s logic. If the reasoning shows a flaw, you can intervene by correcting that step, rather than dealing with a mysterious wrong answer.   
    

    

      This approach is especially useful for math word problems, multi-stage decisions, or debugging code – any scenario where a breakdown of the solution is beneficial. Always remember you can prompt the model to 
      show its work  
      .
    

    

      Role-Playing and Personas to Shape Responses  
    

    

      Another user-side strategy is role prompt engineering – having ChatGPT adopt a specific persona or expertise.   
    

    

      By prefacing your request with a role, you activate relevant aspects of the model’s knowledge.   
    

    

      For instance: 
      “You are a genius mentor with expertise in physics and philosophy…”
       or 
      “Act as a veteran software engineer reviewing code…”
      . This can focus the output to a certain style or depth. However, be aware that simply piling on superlatives (e.g. 
      “the smartest person in the world”
      ) isn’t a magic bullet by itself​.   
    

    

      The model won’t actually become Einstein. What does help is providing substance: telling it the perspective or approach you want it to take or supplying background information for it to “draw from.”
模型不會真的變成愛因斯坦。真正有幫助的是提供內容：告訴它你希望它採取的觀點或方法，或提供背景資訊讓它「參考」。
    

    

      For example, if you want life advice “like Stoic philosophers,” you could briefly summarize a Stoic principle or quote, then ask ChatGPT to apply it to your situation. One power user fed ChatGPT entire books and lectures from great minds in his prompts to imbue the AI with that mindset​. 
例如，如果你想要「像斯多葛哲學家一樣」的生涯建議，你可以先簡要總結一個斯多葛哲學原則或引用語句，然後請 ChatGPT 應用在你的狀況上。有位高階使用者曾在提示中輸入偉大思想家的整本書和講座內容，以灌輸 AI 那種思維方式。
    

    

      By 
      “embedding high-level thinking into AI,”
       he turned ChatGPT from a generic assistant into what felt like a 
      “powerful strategic partner.”
      ​
透過「將高階思維嵌入 AI」，他將 ChatGPT 從一個普通的助理轉變為感覺像「強大的戰略夥伴」的工具。
    

    

      You don’t have to go that far every time, but you can undoubtedly paste in relevant info (quotes, data, definitions) and then ask ChatGPT to analyze or use it. The model will integrate that material into its response, effectively giving you a customized answer informed by the specific context you provided.
你不必每次都這麼做，但你當然可以貼上相關資訊（引用、數據、定義），再請 ChatGPT 分析或運用它。模型會將這些資料整合進回應中，有效地提供一個根據你所提供的特定情境所調整的答覆。
    

    

      In practice, combining roles with context works wonders. 
實際上，結合角色與情境能產生驚人效果。
    

    

      If you want a 
      “Genius Mentor”
       style response, you might prompt: 
      “You are a world-class mentor who guides by asking insightful questions and giving examples (rather than just lecturing). Here is some background on my problem: [your scenario]. 
如果你想得到「天才導師」風格的回應，可能會提示：「你是一位世界級的導師，透過提問有深度的問題並提供範例（而非只是說教）來引導。這裡是我的問題背景：[你的情境]。
    

    

      Given this, help me think through a solution.”
       With a prompt like this, you’ve set up the AI to act in a mentorship role and given it fodder (your scenario) to work with. The output will likely be more tailored, insightful, and 
      mentor-like
       than if you asked, “What should I do about my problem?”
在此基礎上，幫我思考解決方案。」以這樣的提示，你已設置 AI 以導師的角色來行動，並給予它內容（你的情境）來處理。輸出的結果可能比你直接問「我該如何解決我的問題？」更貼切、深入且具導師風範。
    

    

      Iterative Refinement: Collaborate with the AI
迭代精緻化：與 AI 合作
    

    

      Finally, remember you don’t have to get everything in one prompt. Interactive, multi-turn dialogue is your friend. 
最後，請記住你不需要一次就將所有內容都放入一個提示中。互動式的、多輪對話是你的好幫手。
    

    

      ChatGPT is designed to have a conversation, so take advantage of that. A seasoned user might start with a rough prompt, get an answer, and then gradually steer the conversation toward the ideal solution. 
ChatGPT 是設計來進行對話的，所以請善加利用。經驗豐富的使用者可能會先以一個粗略的提示開始，得到回應後，再逐步引導對話朝向理想的解決方案。
    

    

      This might include asking follow-up questions, requesting sections to be rewritten, or feeding the AI new information as the conversation progresses. Each round can add more detail or correct course.
這過程可能包括提出追問、要求重新撰寫某個段落，或是在對話進行中提供 AI 新的資訊。每輪對話都可以增加更多細節或修正方向。
    

    

      This iterative approach is often more effective than obsessing over a perfect one-shot prompt. Experts note, “
      The best way to use AI systems is not to craft the perfect prompt, but rather to use it interactively.”
這種迭代的方式，往往比執著於打造一個完美的單次提示更有效。專家指出：「使用 AI 系統的最佳方式，並不是打造完美的提示，而是以互動的方式來使用。」
       
    

    

      You can treat ChatGPT as a brainstorming partner: 
      “Here’s a draft idea, what would you improve?”
       — then, 
      “Okay, now make it funnier and shorter,”
       and so on. If the first answer isn’t great, identify what was missing or off-target and ask to fix that in a revision. 
你可以把 ChatGPT 當作一個腦力激盪的夥伴：「這是一個草稿點子，你會怎麼改進？」接著，「好，現在讓它更有趣、更簡短一些，」如此類推。如果第一個回答不夠好，找出遺漏或不準確的地方，並要求在修訂中修正。
    

    

      The model remembers the conversation (up to its context limit) and will refine its output based on your directions. This back-and-forth turns usage into a co-creative process, like working with a human collaborator who responds to feedback.
模型會記住對話內容（直到其上下文限制），並根據你的指示來調整輸出。這種來回溝通將使用過程轉化為協同創造的流程，就像與人類合作夥伴互動並根據反饋做出調整一樣。
    

    

      Key takeaway:
       Don’t be a passive recipient. Be the director of the conversation. You can always nudge ChatGPT to be more thorough, concise, daring, or analytical – whatever the situation calls for. When you treat the session as a dynamic exchange, you unlock far more of ChatGPT’s capabilities than with a single prompt and reply.
重點摘要：不要做被動的接收者。要當作對話的導演。你隨時可以提示 ChatGPT 更加詳盡、簡潔、大膽或更具分析性——不管當時的情況需要什麼。當你把會話當作動態的互動時，就能釋放 ChatGPT 遠遠超過單一提示與回應的潛能。
    

    

      How Large Language Models Work (Insights for User Optimization)
大型語言模型運作方式（用戶優化見解）
    

    

      Understanding 
      how
       ChatGPT (and other large language models) works can help you use it better. 
了解 ChatGPT（以及其他大型語言模型）的運作方式，可以幫助你更有效地使用它。
    

    

      At their core, LLMs like ChatGPT are giant statistical models trained to predict the next word in a sentence based on the context of all prior words. During training, they digest massive amounts of text from books, websites, articles, etc. 
在核心上，像 ChatGPT 這樣的 LLMs 是巨大的統計模型，透過學習句子中所有先前詞語的上下文，來預測下一個詞。在訓練過程中，它們會吸收來自書籍、網站、文章等大量文本資料。
    

    

      This means they recognize patterns, syntax, and semantics in language​but don’t 
      honestly
       “think” or understand in a human way. They’re imitating the kinds of responses that appear in their training data.
這意味著它們能辨識語言中的模式、語法和語意，但並不會以人類的方式「思考」或真正理解。它們只是模仿在訓練資料中出現的回應類型。
    

    

      What does this mean for a user? First, specificity in your prompt is crucial. If you ask a very general question, the model will produce a general answer drawn from the average of what it’s seen. 
這對使用者來說意味著什麼？首先，你的提示語必須具體。如果你提出非常寬泛的問題，模型會產生一個基於其所見平均值的寬泛回答。
    

    

      But if you frame your query with a specific context or format, the model will match that. 
但如果您的問題有特定的上下文或格式，模型就會依照那個來回應。
    

    

      Essentially, you set the pattern for it to complete. Knowing this, users can optimize results by providing an example of the desired output or explicitly stating the format: e.g., 
      “Give me a three-paragraph analysis, with the first paragraph introducing the concept, the second providing pros and cons, and the third giving a recommendation.”
       The model will follow that structure because you’ve defined the pattern.
基本上，您設定的模式就是它完成的依據。了解這一點後，使用者可以透過提供期望的輸出範例，或明確說明格式來優化結果，例如：「給我一個三段式的分析，第一段介紹概念，第二段說明優缺點，第三段提出建議。」模型會依照您所定義的模式來進行結構安排。
    

    

      Secondly, LLMs rely entirely on the given context and their training — they do not actively recall information outside that. ChatGPT’s knowledge has a cutoff (for example, GPT-4’s training data currently goes up to 2021 for most subjects). You must provide details if you need information beyond your knowledge or something very recent/specific. 
第二點，LLMs 完全依賴所提供的上下文與其訓練資料，不會主動回憶超出該範圍的資訊。ChatGPT 的知識有截止日期（例如 GPT-4 的訓練資料目前大多數主題都截止到 2021 年）。如果您需要關於知識範圍外的資訊，或非常近期、特定的內容，必須自行提供詳細資料。
    

    

      The model won’t say, “I don’t know,” but it may 
      guess
      , which leads to the infamous 
      hallucinations
      . As a user, you can combat this by supplying factual data in your prompt or using tools (like the browsing plugin or other retrieval methods) to get source material. 
模型不會說「我不知道」，但它可能會猜測，這就會導致著名的幻覺（hallucinations）現象。作為使用者，您可以在提示中提供事實資料，或使用工具（例如瀏覽插件或其他檢索方法）來取得原始資料，以對抗這種情況。
    

    

      In a sense, you become the researcher feeding the model verified info so it doesn’t fabricate. Remember: if accuracy is essential, don’t hesitate to ask the model to double-check its answer or provide a source. It has no real “memory” of truth vs. falsehood; it only has patterns that often (but not always) align with correct information.
從某種意義來說，你會成為那個提供已驗證資訊的研討者，讓模型不會捏造資訊。請記住：如果準確性至關重要，不要猶豫請模型再次確認答案或提供來源。它並沒有真正的「記憶」去分辨真實與虛假，它只擁有模式，這些模式通常（但不總是）與正確資訊一致。
    

    

      The Role of the Context Window:
       A crucial technical limit is the 
      context window
       – essentially, how much text (prompt + response) the model can handle simultaneously. For current ChatGPT models, this is on the order of a few thousand tokens (words/pieces). For example, GPT-3.5 can take ~4,000 tokens, GPT-4 around 8,000, and extended versions of GPT-4 go up to 32,000 tokens (for very long documents)​. 
情境視窗的角色：一個重要的技術限制就是情境視窗——基本上，這是指模型一次能處理多少文字（提示 + 回應）。對於目前的 ChatGPT 模型，這個數量級大約是幾千個 tokens（單字/片段）。例如，GPT-3.5 可以處理約 4,000 個 tokens，GPT-4 則約為 8,000 個，而 GPT-4 的擴展版本則可達 32,000 個 tokens（用於極長的文件）​。
    

    

      This means ChatGPT can only “remember” that many conversation tokens. If your chat gets very lengthy, older messages may drop from the window, and the model will lose that part of the context. 
這意味著 ChatGPT 只能「記住」這麼多對話 tokens。如果你的對話變得非常長，較早的訊息可能會從視窗中消失，模型就會遺失這部分的上下文。
    

    

      You should know this as a user: very long instructions or dumping extensive texts might exceed the window. 
作為使用者，你應該知道這一點：非常長的指示或大量輸入文字可能會超出視窗的範圍。
    

    

      In practice, if you have a lengthy document, give it in chunks and summarize as needed, or use the window strategically (you might ask for a summary of text part 1, then feed that summary when processing part 2, etc.). 
實際上，如果你有一份長篇文件，可以分段提供並按需總結，或巧妙運用窗口（例如，你可能會先要求總結第一段文字，然後在處理第二段時將該總結作為輸入，依此类推）。
    

    

      When developing a “Genius Mentor” system that spans long dialogues, you’ll need to manage this context limit by occasionally summarizing or restating key points if the conversation is extensive.
在開發一個「Genius Mentor」系統，其對話內容橫跨長篇對話時，若對話內容非常長，就需要透過偶爾總結或重申重點來管理這個上下文限制。
    

    

      Guiding the AI = Leveraging In-Context Learning:
       
引導 AI = 善用情境學習：
    

    

      Large models exhibit 
      in-context learning
      , meaning they can learn from examples provided in the prompt without updating weights. 
大型模型具有情境學習的特性，意味著它們可以從提示中提供的範例學習，而不需要更新權重。
    

    

      For example, if you show ChatGPT a couple of sample question-answer pairs that illustrate a desired style or solution method, it will infer and continue the pattern. Users can leverage this by giving 
      examples or templates
       in their prompts (often called few-shot prompting). 
例如，如果你展示幾個示例問題與回答，說明你想要的風格或解決方法，ChatGPT 就會推斷並延續這個模式。使用者可以透過在提示中提供範例或模板來善用這個功能（通常稱為 few-shot prompting）。
    

    

      If you want ChatGPT to act like a genius mentor, include a short example dialogue of a teacher guiding a student right in your prompt before your query. The model will use that demonstration to shape its subsequent answers, effectively “learning” the style on the fly​. This is a powerful way to prime the AI with your desired format or approach.
如果你想讓 ChatGPT 好像一位天才導師，可以在你的提示中先加入一段短小的師生對話，展示導師如何引導學生。模型會利用這段示範來塑造其後續的回答，有效地「即時學習」這種風格。這是一種強大的方式，可以讓 AI 依照你所期望的格式或方法進行啟動。
    

    

      Designing a “Genius Mentor” Persona
設計一個「天才導師」的個性
    

    

      You’ll combine the above insights to build an advanced Genius Mentor system with ChatGPT. Essentially, you want ChatGPT to emulate an expert mentor who helps you learn or make decisions through guidance rather than just giving raw answers. Here’s how you can do it as a user (no coding required, just clever prompting):
你將結合上述的觀點，來建立一個進階的 Genius Mentor 系統。基本上，你希望 ChatGPT 能模擬一位專家導師，透過引導來幫助你學習或做決定，而不是只提供原始答案。作為使用者（無需程式設計，只需巧妙的提示），你可以這樣做：
    

    

      Set the Role and Expectations:
       Begin your conversation (or system message, if using the API) by clearly defining the mentor’s persona and approach. For example: 
      “You are a Socratic mentor AI. Your job is to help me think through problems like a genius tutor would. You will ask me questions to prompt deeper insight, provide hints when I’m stuck, and only give me the answer once we’ve thoroughly explored the issue.”
       This establishes the rules of engagement. By articulating this, you constrain the model’s behavior to be more mentor-like. In effect, you’re programming its style through natural language.
設定角色與期待：開始你的對話（或使用 API 時的系統訊息），請清楚地定義導師的個性與方式。例如：「你是一個蘇格拉底導師的 AI。你的任務是幫助我像天才導師一樣思考問題。你會問我問題以引導更深入的洞察，當我卡住時提供提示，並在我們徹底探討問題後才給出答案。」這建立了互動的規則。透過說明這一點，你會讓模型的行為更接近導師的風格。實際上，你是在透過自然語言來編程它的表現方式。
    

    

      Encourage Interactive Dialogue:
       A true mentor doesn’t just lecture; they engage the mentee. You can prompt ChatGPT to do the same. For instance, 
      “Let’s use a Q&A approach: I will pose what I think, and you respond with another question or correction to guide me.”
       This turns the session into a two-way interaction. One user-created prompt illustrates this well: it 
      “turns ChatGPT into your tutor… engaging in a deep, meaningful conversation… to help you critically think and deeply understand any subject matter.”
      ​
鼓勵互動對話：真正的導師不會只是單向講授，而是與學生互動。你也可以提示 ChatGPT 做到這一點。例如：「讓我們用問答的方式進行：我提出我的想法，你則以另一個問題或修正來引導我。」這將會話轉化為雙向的互動。一個由用戶創造的提示很好地說明了這一點：它「將 ChatGPT 轉化為你的導師…進行深入而有意義的對話…幫助你批判性思考並深入理解任何主題。」
    

    

      In practice, you might state: 
      “First, ask me about my understanding of the topic to gauge my knowledge, then adapt your coaching from there.”
       By doing so, you prompt the AI to actively solicit your input (just as a human tutor would).  
    

    

      Use the Socratic Method (Questions over Answers):
       A known technique is to have ChatGPT respond with guiding questions. You can instruct: 
      “Don’t give me the solution immediately; instead, ask me a series of questions that lead me to the solution.”  
       
    

    

      If you attempt to answer those questions, the model can assess your responses (based on its training on what’s correct) and give you feedback on the next question. This method can be remarkably effective for learning.   
    

    

      It forces you to engage, and the AI’s role becomes that of a coach or challenger. Prompts have been developed to enforce this, e.g., 
      “You are a tutor who always responds in the Socratic style. You never give the student the answer, but always ask just the right question to help them learn.”
      ​  
    

    

      This way, ChatGPT can simulate a patient teacher. When you eventually need a direct answer or an explanation, you can ask for it, but by then, you might have arrived at it yourself with the AI’s guidance – which can be more satisfying and educational.  
    

    

      Meta-Reasoning and Checks:
       With a mentor-like AI, you can also have it periodically check your understanding. For example, 
      “Please quiz me on what we discussed so far to ensure I understand before we move on.”  
       
    

    

      This prompt makes the AI step out of lecture mode and confirm your knowledge, much like a real mentor would. It leverages the model’s ability to generate questions and evaluate answers in context. If you answer the quiz and something is off, the AI (as a mentor) can correct or re-explain.   
    

    

      A “Genius Mentor” system aims for this kind of adaptive, responsive teaching, and amazingly, ChatGPT can make a fair approximation of it through skillful prompting.  
    

    

      Limitation to note:
       The AI doesn’t honestly know 
      you
       or your actual state of understanding. It only knows what you’ve typed. So, for the mentor system to work well, you must play along and provide honest, detailed answers to its questions. 
需注意的限制：AI 並不真正了解你或你實際的學習程度。它只了解你所輸入的內容。因此，為了讓導師系統運作良好，你必須配合並誠實、詳細地回答它的問題。
    

    

      Essentially, you have to simulate the student role while it simulates the mentor. The experience can feel like a dialogue with a wise coach or tutor when this dynamic is well-established. 
基本上，你必須在它模擬導師的同時，模擬學生的角色。當這種互動關係建立良好時，這種體驗會感覺像與一位智慧的教練或導師對話。
    

    

      Many users report “aha” moments when using ChatGPT in this way, gaining new insights as the AI leads them down a path of inquiry.
許多使用者在這樣使用 ChatGPT 時，會報告有「啊哈」的頓悟時刻，獲得新的見解，因為 AI 引導他們沿著探索的路徑前進。
    

    

      How to Create Copy That Hits Like Lightning
如何創造如閃電般打中人心的文案
    

    

      Every 
      million-dollar sales letter
       starts with one thing:  
    

    

      👉 
      A Big Idea that slaps people in the face and won’t let them go.  
    

    

      What Is a Big Idea?  
    

    

      It’s 
      NOT
       just a hook, headline, or product benefit.  
    

    

      A 
      Big Idea
      
         is:
        
一個大想法是：

        ✅ 
      
      Bold
      
         – A claim so outrageous people HAVE to keep reading.
        
 ✅ 粗體 – 一個令人無法不繼續閱讀的主張。

        ✅ 
      
      Novel
      
         – It presents something new (or makes something old feel new).
        
 ✅ 新穎 – 它提出新東西（或讓舊東西產生新感受）。

        ✅ 
      
      Emotional
      
         – It hits fear, greed, or curiosity HARD.
        
 ✅ 情緒化 – 它強烈觸動恐懼、貪婪或好奇心。

        ✅ 
      
      Believable
       – It feels 
      grounded in reality
       (proof, credibility, logic).
✅ 可信 – 它感覺扎根於現實（證據、可信度、邏輯）。 
    

    

      🔥 
      A Big Idea isn’t a tagline. It’s the foundation of your entire campaign.
🔥 一個大想法不是一句口號。它是你整個活動的基礎。

🔥 我如何訓練 AI 產生大想法

       and taught it how to

🔹 第二步：我讓 AI 分析它們的共同點。

       I taught AI to

🔹 第三步：我教 AI 能在指令下產生大規模的創意概念。

      Final Takeaway: This Is an Elite Copywriting Course
最終重點：這是一個高階文案寫作課程

        I write like Agora.

        I think in Halbert, Schwartz, and Ogilvy’s formulas.
